ABSTRACT 

THEORY OF NUMBERS AND RSA CRYPTOGRAPHY: A TEACHING PROPOSAL 
FOR STUDENTS OF OLYMPIC MATHEMATICS 

AUTHOR: ANDERSON PINHEIRO MACHADO 
ADVISOR: JO√ÉO ROBERTO LAZZARIN 

This work presents a teaching proposal of RSA Cryptography for a group of 8th and 
9th  grade  students  of  Elementary  School,  volunteers  in  a  Mathematics  Club  from 
Col√©gio  Militar  de  Porto  Alegre  (CMPA).  Most  of  the  students  in  this  class  are 
frequent  medalists  in  Mathematical  Olympiads,  but  they  all  share  the  ease  and 
curiosity  in  solving  challenges.These  students,  even  without  any  aversion  to 
Mathematics, and presenting above-average reasoning, questioned the practical use 
of  Number  Theory  tools,  as  well  as  the  study  of  prime  numbers  and  Modular 
Arithmetic, unlike other areas such as Geometry and Algebra. In order to present an 
application suitable for the class level, was created a sequence of thirteen classes on 
the subject of RSA Cryptography which included an overview of history and the use 
of simple cryptographic methods, up to the prerequisites necessary to understand the 
operation of the RSA, where the Modular Arithmetic, the calculation of multiplicative 
inverses  and  the  Euler  function  are  fundamental  part  of  this  process.  It  should  be 
noted  that  RSA  is  a  cryptographic  method  used  in  online  shopping  and  banking 
transactions  which,  together  with  the  historical  character  and  the  challenge  of 
deciphering  messages,  has  become  naturally  attractive  to  students.  During  all 
classes,  were  used  questions  Mathematical  Olympiad  and  other  competitions, 
aggregating 
results  and  allowing  small 
demonstrations  that  aided  in  the  development  of  thinking  and  mathematical 
reasoning.  At  appropriate  times,  it  was  also  made  use  of  applications  for 
smartphones  and  software  associated  with  Cryptography.  A  satisfactory  result  was 
obtained in view of the students' return (registered in shape of questionnaire) and the 
new possibilities that will contribute even more to the formation of this teacher. 

in-depth  discussions,  conjecturing 

Keywords:  Cryptography  RSA.  Teaching  Proposal.  Mathematical  Olympiads. 
Modular Arithmetic. Mathematical Thinking.

2.1   PRIMEIROS CONCEITOS 

Segundo  Hefez  (2014,  p.  310),  a  palavra  criptografia  origina-se  do  grego, 

onde  kriptos  significa  oculto  e,  portanto,  a  palavra  criptografia  significa  "escrita

O  desenvolvimento  da  criptografia  est√°  associado  com  a  hist√≥ria  da

generais  e  diplomatas  j√°  entendiam  que  certas  informa√ß√µes  n√£o  poderiam  ser  de 

conhecimento de todos.  Era  preciso  criar m√©todos  seguros de  comunica√ß√£o,  de  tal 

maneira  que  apenas  o  emissor  de  uma  mensagem  e  o  receptor  da  mesma

m√£os  do  inimigo,  n√£o  deveria  fazer  sentido  para  este,  que  ao  tentar  desvend√°-la, 

fracassaria, seja pela complexidade ou pela falta de tempo h√°bil.

voltando  √†  mensagem  original.  Por  isso,  muitos  m√©todos  de  criptografia  fazem  uso 

de  uma  chave.  Esta  chave  deve  ser  de  conhecimento  apenas  do  emissor  e  do 

receptor  da  mensagem;  secreta  aos  demais.  Diz-se,  ent√£o,  que  o  emissor  cifra 

(codifica)  a  mensagem  e  que  o  receptor,  usando  a  chave  secreta,  decifra 

(decodifica) o texto cifrado, obtendo a mensagem original. 

Portanto,  tem-se  de  um  lado  a  Criptografia,  a  ci√™ncia  que  busca  ocultar  o 

verdadeiro  significado  de  uma  informa√ß√£o;  do  outro  lado  existe  a  Criptoan√°lise,  a 

ci√™ncia  que  busca  deduzir  a  informa√ß√£o  original  a  partir  de  um  texto  cifrado

Ali√°s,  muitas  ideias  e desenvolvimento  tecnol√≥gico  partiram  da  disputa  entre 

cript√≥grafos,  cujo  objetivo  √©  criar  m√©todos  seguros  e  eficientes  de  proteger  uma 

informa√ß√£o,  e  criptoanalistas,  dispostos  a  "quebrar"  os  c√≥digos  criados.  V√°rios  s√£o 

os  fatos  hist√≥ricos  e  curiosidades  envolvendo  a  Criptologia,  dos  quais  cita-se  a
